The IDA mechanism involves a host molecule bound to an electroactive indicator; when quinine is introduced, it displaces the indicator, leading to a measurable electrochemical signal. The calibration curve (signal vs. quinine concentration) is constructed to determine the sensor's sensitivity and linear range.\n\n2. **Selectivity**: The sensor's response to quinine is compared to its response to structurally similar compounds or potential interferents. This ensures that the IDA is selective for quinine and not significantly affected by other substances.\n\n3. **Reproducibility and Stability**: Multiple measurements are performed with the same and different sensor batches to assess reproducibility. The sensor's stability over time and under different storage conditions is also evaluated.\n\n4. **Limit of Detection (LOD) and Limit of Quantification (LOQ)**: These parameters are determined to establish the lowest concentration of quinine that can be reliably detected and quantified by the sensor.\n\n5. **Comparison with Reference Methods**: The sensor's results are compared with those pharmaceutical formulations) to demonstrate its practical applicability and robustness in complex matrices.\n\nThrough these steps, the electrochemical IDA sensor for quinine is thoroughly verified,
